        <h3> 
         <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-book" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
          <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M3 5h4v1H3V5zm0 3h4V7H3v1zm0 2h4V9H3v1zm11-5h-4v1h4V5zm0 2h-4v1h4V7zm0 2h-4v1h4V9zm2-6v9c0 .55-.45 1-1 1H9.5l-1 1-1-1H2c-.55 0-1-.45-1-1V3c0-.55.45-1 1-1h5.5l1 1 1-1H15c.55 0 1 .45 1 1zm-8 .5L7.5 3H2v9h6V3.5zm7-.5H9.5l-.5.5V12h6V3z" />
         </svg> README.md </h3> 
        <article class="markdown-body entry-content" itemprop="text">
         <h1><a id="user-content-everyauth" class="anchor" href="#everyauth" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>everyauth</h1> 
         <p>Authentication and authorization (password, facebook, &amp; more) for your node.js Connect and Express apps.</p> 
         <p>There is a NodeTuts screencast of everyauth <a href="http://vimeo.com/26532298">here</a></p> 
         <p>There is also a Google Groups (recently created) <a href="http://groups.google.com/group/everyauth">here</a> to post questions and discuss potential ideas and extensions to the library.</p> 
         <p>So far, <code>everyauth</code> enables you to login via:</p>

         <p><code>everyauth</code> is:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><strong>Modular</strong> - We have you covered with Facebook and Twitter OAuth logins, basic login/password support, and modules coming soon for beta invitation support and more.</li> 
          <li><strong>Easily Configurable</strong> - everyauth was built with powerful configuration needs in mind. Configure an authorization strategy in a straightforward, easy-to-read &amp; easy-to-write approach, with as much granularity as you want over the steps and logic of your authorization strategy.</li> 
          <li><strong>Idiomatic</strong> - The syntax for configuring and extending your authorization strategies are idiomatic and chainable.</li> 
         </ul> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-installation" class="anchor" href="#installation" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Installation</h2> 
         <pre><code>$ npm install everyauth
</code></pre> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-quick-start" class="anchor" href="#quick-start" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Quick Start</h2> 
         <p>Incorporate everyauth into your express app in just 2 easy steps.</p> 
         <ol> 
          <li> <p><strong>Choose and Configure Auth Strategies</strong> - Find the authentication strategy you desire in one of the sections below. Follow the configuration instructions.</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><strong>Add the Middleware to Express</strong></p> 
           <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
            <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> everyauth <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>everyauth<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Step 1 code goes here</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Step 2 code</span>
<span class="pl-k">var</span> express <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>express<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
<span class="pl-k">var</span> app <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-en">express</span>();
app
  .<span class="pl-en">use</span>(<span class="pl-smi">express</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>())
  .<span class="pl-en">use</span>(<span class="pl-smi">express</span>.<span class="pl-en">cookieParser</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>mr ripley<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>))
  .<span class="pl-en">use</span>(<span class="pl-smi">express</span>.<span class="pl-en">session</span>())
  .<span class="pl-en">use</span>(<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">middleware</span>(app));</pre>
           </div> </li> 
         </ol> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-example-application" class="anchor" href="#example-application" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Example Application</h2> 
         <p>There is an example application at <a href="https://github.com/bnoguchi/everyauth/tree/master/example">./example</a></p> 
         <p>To run it:</p> 
         <pre><code>$ cd example
$ node server.js
</code></pre> 
         <p><strong>Important</strong> - Some OAuth Providers do not allow callbacks to localhost, so you will need to create a <code>localhost</code> alias called <code>local.host</code>. Make sure you set up your /etc/hosts so that 127.0.0.1 is also associated with 'local.host'. So inside your /etc/hosts file, one of the lines will look like:</p> 
         <pre><code>127.0.0.1	localhost local.host
</code></pre> 
         <p>Then point your browser to <a href="http://local.host:3000">http://local.host:3000</a></p> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-tests" class="anchor" href="#tests" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Tests</h2> 
         <pre><code>$ npm install everyauth --dev
</code></pre> 
         <p>Then, update test/creds.js with credentials that the integration tests use to login to each 3rd party service.</p> 
         <pre><code>$ make test
</code></pre> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-accessing-the-user" class="anchor" href="#accessing-the-user" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Accessing the User</h2> 
         <p>If you are using <code>express</code> or <code>connect</code>, then <code>everyauth</code> provides an easy way to access the user as:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>req.user</code> from your app server</li> 
          <li><code>everyauth.user</code> via the <code>everyauth</code> helper accessible from your <code>express</code> views.</li> 
          <li><code>user</code> as a helper accessible from your <code>express</code> views</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>To access the user, configure <code>everyauth.everymodule.findUserById</code> and optionally <code>everyauth.everymodule.userPkey</code>. For example, using <a href="http://github.com/LearnBoost/mongoose">mongoose</a>:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>.<span class="pl-en">findUserById</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">userId</span>, <span class="pl-smi">callback</span>) {
  <span class="pl-smi">User</span>.<span class="pl-en">findById</span>(userId, callback);
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> callback has the signature, function (err, user) {...}</span>
});</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>If you need access to the request object the function can have three arguments:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>.<span class="pl-en">findUserById</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>, <span class="pl-smi">userId</span>, <span class="pl-smi">callback</span>) {

  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> use the request in some way ...</span>

  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> callback has the signature, function (err, user) {...}</span>
});</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>Once you have configured this method, you now have access to the user object that was fetched anywhere in your server app code as <code>req.user</code>. For instance:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> app <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>express<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>).<span class="pl-en">createServer</span>()

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Configure your app</span>

<span class="pl-smi">app</span>.<span class="pl-c1">get</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>, <span class="pl-smi">res</span>) {
  <span class="pl-en">console</span>.<span class="pl-c1">log</span>(<span class="pl-smi">req</span>.<span class="pl-smi">user</span>);  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> FTW!</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">res</span>.<span class="pl-en">render</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>home<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
});</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>Moreover, you can access the user in your views as <code>everyauth.user</code> or as <code>user</code>.</p> 
         <pre><code>//- Inside ./views/home.jade
span.user-id= everyauth.user.name
#user-id= user.id
</code></pre> 
         <p><code>everyauth</code> assumes that you store your users with an <code>id</code> property. If not -- e.g, if you adopt the convention <code>user.uid</code> over <code>user.id</code> -- then just make sure to configure the <code>everyauth.everymodule.userPkey</code> parameter:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>.<span class="pl-en">userPkey</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>uid<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-express-helpers" class="anchor" href="#express-helpers" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Express Helpers</h2> 
         <p>If you are using express, everyauth comes with some useful dynamic helpers. To enable them:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> express <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>express<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  , everyauth <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>everyauth<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  , app <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">express</span>.<span class="pl-en">createServer</span>();

<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">helpExpress</span>(app);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>Then, from within your views, you will have access to the following helpers methods attached to the helper, <code>everyauth</code>:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>everyauth.loggedIn</code></li> 
          <li><code>everyauth.user</code> - the User document associated with the session</li> 
          <li><code>everyauth.facebook</code> - The is equivalent to what is stored at <code>req.session.auth.facebook</code>, so you can do things like ...</li> 
          <li><code>everyauth.facebook.user</code> - returns the user json provided from the OAuth provider.</li> 
          <li><code>everyauth.facebook.accessToken</code> - returns the access_token provided from the OAuth provider for authorized API calls on behalf of the user.</li> 
          <li>And you also get this pattern for other modules - e.g., <code>everyauth.twitter.user</code>, <code>everyauth.github.user</code>, etc.</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>You also get access to the view helper</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>user</code> - the same as <code>everyauth.user</code> above</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>As an example of how you would use these, consider the following <code>./views/user.jade</code> jade template:</p> 
         <pre><code>.user-id
  .label User Id
  .value #{user.id}
.facebook-id
  .label User Facebook Id
  .value #{everyauth.facebook.user.id}
</code></pre> 
         <p>If you already have an express helper named <code>user</code>, then you can configure <code>everyauth</code> to use a different helper name to access the user object that everyauth manages. To do so, leverage the <code>userAlias</code> option for <code>everyauth.helpExpress</code>:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">helpExpress</span>(app, { userAlias<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>__user__<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> });</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>Then, you could access the user object in your view with the helper <code>__user__</code> instead of the default helper <code>user</code>. So you can compare with the default use of helpers given previously, the alternative leveraging userAlias would look like:</p> 
         <pre><code>.user-id
  .label User Id
  .value #{__user__.id}
.facebook-id
  .label User Facebook Id
  .value #{everyauth.facebook.user.id}
</code></pre> 
         <p><code>everyauth</code> also provides convenience methods on the <code>ServerRequest</code> instance <code>req</code>. From any scope that has access to <code>req</code>, you get the following convenience getters and methods:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>req.loggedIn</code> - a Boolean getter that tells you if the request is by a logged in user</li> 
          <li><code>req.user</code> - the User document associated with the session</li> 
          <li><code>req.logout()</code> - clears the session of your auth data</li> 
         </ul> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-logging-out" class="anchor" href="#logging-out" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Logging Out</h2> 
         <p>If you integrate <code>everyauth</code> with <code>connect</code>, then <code>everyauth</code> automatically sets up a <code>logoutPath</code> at <code>GET</code> <code>/logout</code> for your app. It also sets a default handler for your logout route that clears your session of auth information and redirects them to '/'.</p> 
         <p>To over-write the logout path:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>.<span class="pl-en">logoutPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/bye<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>To over-write the logout redirect path:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>.<span class="pl-en">logoutRedirectPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/navigate/to/after/logout<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>To over-write the logout handler:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>.<span class="pl-en">handleLogout</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>, <span class="pl-smi">res</span>) {
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Put you extra logic here</span>
  
  <span class="pl-smi">req</span>.<span class="pl-en">logout</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> The logout method is added for you by everyauth, too</span>
  
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> And/or put your extra logic here</span>
  
  <span class="pl-c1">this</span>.<span class="pl-en">redirect</span>(res, <span class="pl-c1">this</span>.<span class="pl-en">logoutRedirectPath</span>());
});</pre>
         </div> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-custom-redirect-on-password-based-login-or-registration" class="anchor" href="#custom-redirect-on-password-based-login-or-registration" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Custom redirect on password-based login or registration</h2> 
         <p>You may want your own callback that decides where to send a user after login or registration. One way of doing this is with the <code>respondToLoginSucceed</code> and <code>respondToRegistrationSucceed</code> methods. This assumes that you have set a <code>.redirectTo</code> property on your <code>req.session</code> object:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">respondToLoginSucceed</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">res</span>, <span class="pl-smi">user</span>, <span class="pl-smi">data</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> (user) {
      <span class="pl-c1">this</span>.<span class="pl-en">redirect</span>(res, <span class="pl-smi">data</span>.<span class="pl-smi">session</span>.<span class="pl-smi">redirectTo</span>)
    }   
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">respondToRegistrationSucceed</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">res</span>, <span class="pl-smi">user</span>, <span class="pl-smi">data</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c1">this</span>.<span class="pl-en">redirect</span>(res, <span class="pl-smi">data</span>.<span class="pl-smi">session</span>.<span class="pl-smi">redirectTo</span>)
  })</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>If you are using express and want your redirects to be subject to <a href="http://expressjs.com/guide.html#res.redirect()">express redirect mapping</a>, you can overwrite redirect method employed by everyauth.</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">everymodule</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">performRedirect</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">res</span>, <span class="pl-smi">location</span>) {
    <span class="pl-smi">res</span>.<span class="pl-en">redirect</span>(location, <span class="pl-c1">303</span>);
  });</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>A newly defined method will be used by everyauth to perform all redirects.</p> 
         <h1><a id="user-content-auth-strategy-instructions" class="anchor" href="#auth-strategy-instructions" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Auth Strategy Instructions</h1> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-facebook-connect" class="anchor" href="#facebook-connect" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Facebook Connect</h2> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> everyauth <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>everyauth<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  , connect <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>connect<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">appId</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR APP ID HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">appSecret</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR APP SECRET HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">handleAuthCallbackError</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>, <span class="pl-smi">res</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> If a user denies your app, Facebook will redirect the user to</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> /auth/facebook/callback?error_reason=user_denied&amp;error=access_denied&amp;error_description=The+user+denied+your+request.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> This configurable route handler defines how you want to respond to</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> that.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> If you do not configure this, everyauth renders a default fallback</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> view notifying the user that their authentication failed and why.</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">findOrCreateUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">session</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessToken</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessTokExtra</span>, <span class="pl-smi">fbUserMetadata</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> find or create user logic goes here</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">redirectPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">routes</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">app</span>) {
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Define your routes here</span>
};

<span class="pl-en">connect</span>(
    <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">cookieParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">session</span>({secret<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>whodunnit<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>})
  , <span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">middleware</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">router</span>(routes);
).<span class="pl-en">listen</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3000</span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>You can also configure more parameters (most are set to defaults) via the same chainable API:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">entryPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/auth/facebook<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">callbackPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/auth/facebook/callback<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-c1">scope</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)                        <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Defaults to undefined</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">fields</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>id,name,email,picture<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)       <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Controls the returned fields. Defaults to undefined</span></pre>
         </div> 
         <p>If you want to see what the current value of a configured parameter is, you can do so via:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>.<span class="pl-c1">scope</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> undefined</span>
<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>.<span class="pl-en">fields</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> undefined</span>
<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>.<span class="pl-en">entryPath</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> '/auth/facebook'</span></pre>
         </div> 
         <p>To see all parameters that are configurable, the following will return an object whose parameter name keys map to description values:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>.<span class="pl-en">configurable</span>();</pre>
         </div> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-dynamic-facebook-connect-scope" class="anchor" href="#dynamic-facebook-connect-scope" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Dynamic Facebook Connect Scope</h3> 
         <p>Facebook provides many different <a href="http://developers.facebook.com/docs/authentication/permissions/">permissions</a> for which your app can ask your user. This is bundled up in the <code>scope</code> query paremter sent with the oauth request to Facebook. While your app may require several different permissions from Facebook, Facebook recommends that you only ask for these permissions incrementally, as you need them. For example, you might want to only ask for the "email" scope upon registration. At the same time, for another user, you may want to ask for "user_status" permissions because they have progressed further along in your application.</p> 
         <p><code>everyauth</code> enables you to specify the "scope" dynamically with a second variation of the configurable <code>scope</code>. In addition to the first variation that looks like:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>
  .<span class="pl-c1">scope</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>email,user_status<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>you can have greater dynamic control over "scope" via the second variation of <code>scope</code>:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>
  .<span class="pl-c1">scope</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>, <span class="pl-smi">res</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> session <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">req</span>.<span class="pl-smi">session</span>;
    <span class="pl-k">switch</span> (<span class="pl-smi">session</span>.<span class="pl-smi">userPhase</span>) {
      <span class="pl-k">case</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>registration<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>:
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>;
      <span class="pl-k">case</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>share-media<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>:
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>email,user_status<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>;
    }
  });
</pre>
         </div> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-facebook-mobile-oauth-dialog" class="anchor" href="#facebook-mobile-oauth-dialog" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Facebook Mobile OAuth Dialog</h3> 
         <p>If you are programming for mobile, you can bring up the facebook mobile OAuth dialog instead of the traditional desktop browser-based one by just adding <code>mobile(true)</code> to your configuration as seen here:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">facebook</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">mobile</span>(<span class="pl-c1">true</span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">appId</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR APP ID HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">appSecret</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR APP SECRET HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> rest of configuration</span></pre>
         </div> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-twitter-oauth" class="anchor" href="#twitter-oauth" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Twitter OAuth</h2> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> everyauth <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>everyauth<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  , connect <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>connect<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">twitter</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">consumerKey</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR CONSUMER ID HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">consumerSecret</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR CONSUMER SECRET HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">findOrCreateUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">session</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessToken</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessTokenSecret</span>, <span class="pl-smi">twitterUserMetadata</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> find or create user logic goes here</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">redirectPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">routes</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">app</span>) {
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Define your routes here</span>
};

<span class="pl-en">connect</span>(
    <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">cookieParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">session</span>({secret<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>whodunnit<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>})
  , <span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">middleware</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">router</span>(routes);
).<span class="pl-en">listen</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3000</span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p><strong>Important</strong> - Some developers forget to do the following, and it causes them to have issues with <code>everyauth</code>. Please make sure to do the following: When you set up your app at <a href="http://dev.twitter.com/">http://dev.twitter.com/</a>, make sure that your callback url is set up to include that path '/auth/twitter/callback/'. In general, when dealing with OAuth or OAuth2 modules provided by <code>everyauth</code>, the default callback path is always set up to follow the pattern '/auth/#{moduleName}/callback', so just ensure that you configure your OAuth settings accordingly with the OAuth provider -- in this case, the "Edit Application Settings" section for your app at <a href="http://dev.twitter.com">http://dev.twitter.com</a>.</p> 
         <p>Alternatively, you can specify the callback url at the application level by configuring <code>callbackPath</code> (which has a default configuration of "/auth/twitter/callback"):</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">twitter</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">consumerKey</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR CONSUMER ID HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">consumerSecret</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR CONSUMER SECRET HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">callbackPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/custom/twitter/callback/path<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">findOrCreateUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">session</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessToken</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessTokenSecret</span>, <span class="pl-smi">twitterUserMetadata</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> find or create user logic goes here</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">redirectPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>So if your hostname is <code>example.com</code>, then this configuration will over-ride the <code>dev.twitter.com</code> callback url configuration. Instead, Twitter will redirect back to <code>example.com/custom/twitter/callback/path</code> in the example just given above.</p> 
         <p>You can also configure more parameters (most are set to defaults) via the same chainable API:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">twitter</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">entryPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/auth/twitter<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">callbackPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/auth/twitter/callback<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>If you want to see what the current value of a configured parameter is, you can do so via:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">twitter</span>.<span class="pl-en">callbackPath</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> '/auth/twitter/callback'</span>
<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">twitter</span>.<span class="pl-en">entryPath</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> '/auth/twitter'</span></pre>
         </div> 
         <p>To see all parameters that are configurable, the following will return an object whose parameter name keys map to description values:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">twitter</span>.<span class="pl-en">configurable</span>();</pre>
         </div> 
         <h2><a id="user-content-password-authentication" class="anchor" href="#password-authentication" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Password Authentication</h2> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> everyauth <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>everyauth<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  , connect <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>connect<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">getLoginPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/login<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Uri path to the login page</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">postLoginPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/login<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Uri path that your login form POSTs to</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">loginView</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>a string of html; OR the name of the jade/etc-view-engine view<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">authenticate</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">login</span>, <span class="pl-smi">password</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Either, we return a user or an array of errors if doing sync auth.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Or, we return a Promise that can fulfill to promise.fulfill(user) or promise.fulfill(errors)</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> `errors` is an array of error message strings</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> e.g., </span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Example 1 - Sync Example</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> if (usersByLogin[login] &amp;&amp; usersByLogin[login].password === password) {</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   return usersByLogin[login];</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> } else {</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   return ['Login failed'];</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> }</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Example 2 - Async Example</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> var promise = this.Promise()</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> YourUserModel.find({ login: login}, function (err, user) {</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   if (err) return promise.fulfill([err]);</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   promise.fulfill(user);</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> }</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> return promise;</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">loginSuccessRedirect</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Where to redirect to after a login</span>
  
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> If login fails, we render the errors via the login view template,</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> so just make sure your loginView() template incorporates an `errors` local.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> See './example/views/login.jade'</span>

  .<span class="pl-en">getRegisterPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/register<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Uri path to the registration page</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">postRegisterPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/register<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> The Uri path that your registration form POSTs to</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">registerView</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>a string of html; OR the name of the jade/etc-view-engine view<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-en">validateRegistration</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Validate the registration input</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Return undefined, null, or [] if validation succeeds</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Return an array of error messages (or Promise promising this array)</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> if validation fails</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> e.g., assuming you define validate with the following signature</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> var errors = validate(login, password, extraParams);</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> return errors;</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> The `errors` you return show up as an `errors` local in your jade template</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">registerUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> This step is only executed if we pass the validateRegistration step without</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> any errors.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Returns a user (or a Promise that promises a user) after adding it to</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> some user store.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> As an edge case, sometimes your database may make you aware of violation</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> of the unique login index, so if this error is sent back in an async</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> callback, then you can just return that error as a single element array</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> containing just that error message, and everyauth will automatically handle</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> that as a failed registration. Again, you will have access to this error via</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> the `errors` local in your register view jade template.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> e.g.,</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> var promise = this.Promise();</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> User.create(newUserAttributes, function (err, user) {</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   if (err) return promise.fulfill([err]);</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   promise.fulfill(user);</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> });</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> return promise;</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span></span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Note: Index and db-driven validations are the only validations that occur </span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> here; all other validations occur in the `validateRegistration` step documented above.</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">registerSuccessRedirect</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Where to redirect to after a successful registration</span>

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">routes</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">app</span>) {
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Define your routes here</span>
};

<span class="pl-en">connect</span>(
    <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">cookieParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">session</span>({secret<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>whodunnit<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>})
  , <span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">middleware</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">router</span>(routes);
).<span class="pl-en">listen</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3000</span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>You can also configure more parameters (most are set to defaults) via the same chainable API:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">loginFormFieldName</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>login<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)       <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Defaults to 'login'</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">passwordFormFieldName</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Defaults to 'password'</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">loginLayout</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>custom_login_layout<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Only with `express`</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">registerLayout</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>custom reg_layout<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Only with `express`</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">loginLocals</span>(fn);                    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> See Recipe 3 below</span></pre>
         </div> 
         <p>If you want to see what the current value of a configured parameter is, you can do so via:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">loginFormFieldName</span>();    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> 'login'</span>
<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">passwordFormFieldName</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> 'password'</span></pre>
         </div> 
         <p>To see all parameters that are configurable, the following will return an object whose parameter name keys map to description values:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">configurable</span>();</pre>
         </div> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-password-recipe-1-extra-registration-data" class="anchor" href="#password-recipe-1-extra-registration-data" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Password Recipe 1: Extra registration data</h3> 
         <p>Sometimes your registration will ask for more information from the user besides the login and password.</p> 
         <p>For this particular scenario, you can configure the optional step, <code>extractExtraRegistrationParams</code>.</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">extractExtraRegistrationParams</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>) {
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> {
      phone<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-smi">req</span>.<span class="pl-c1">body</span>.<span class="pl-smi">phone</span>
    , name<span class="pl-k">:</span> {
          first<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-smi">req</span>.<span class="pl-c1">body</span>.<span class="pl-smi">first_name</span>
        , last<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-smi">req</span>.<span class="pl-c1">body</span>.<span class="pl-smi">last_name</span>
      }
  };
});</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>Then, you will have access to this data from within your configured <code>validateRegistration</code> and <code>registerUser</code>:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">validateRegistration</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> phone <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>.<span class="pl-smi">phone</span>
      , firstName <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>.<span class="pl-c1">name</span>.<span class="pl-smi">first</span>
      , lastName <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>.<span class="pl-c1">name</span>.<span class="pl-smi">last</span>;
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">registerUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> phone <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>.<span class="pl-smi">phone</span>
      , firstName <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>.<span class="pl-c1">name</span>.<span class="pl-smi">first</span>
      , lastName <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>.<span class="pl-c1">name</span>.<span class="pl-smi">last</span>;
  });</pre>
         </div> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-password-recipe-2-logging-in-with-email-or-phone-number" class="anchor" href="#password-recipe-2-logging-in-with-email-or-phone-number" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Password Recipe 2: Logging in with email or phone number</h3> 
         <p>By default, <code>everyauth</code> uses the field and user key name <code>login</code> during the registration and login process.</p> 
         <p>Sometimes, you want to use <code>email</code> or <code>phone</code> instead of <code>login</code>. Moreover, you also want to validate <code>email</code> and <code>phone</code> fields upon registration.</p> 
         <p><code>everyauth</code> provides an easy way to do this:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">loginWith</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> OR</span>

<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">loginWith</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>phone<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p>With simple login configuration like this, you get email (or phone) validation in addition to renaming of the form field and user key corresponding to what otherwise would typically be referred to as 'login'.</p> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-password-recipe-3-adding-additional-view-local-variables-to-login-and-registration-views" class="anchor" href="#password-recipe-3-adding-additional-view-local-variables-to-login-and-registration-views" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Password Recipe 3: Adding additional view local variables to login and registration views</h3> 
         <p>If you are using <code>express</code>, you are able to pass variables from your app context to your view context via local variables. <code>everyauth</code> provides several convenience local vars for your views, but sometimes you will want to augment this set of local vars with additional locals.</p> 
         <p>So <code>everyauth</code> also provides a mechanism for you to do so via the following configurables:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">loginLocals</span>(<span class="pl-k">...</span>);
<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>.<span class="pl-en">registerLocals</span>(<span class="pl-k">...</span>);</pre>
         </div> 
         <p><code>loginLocals</code> and <code>registerLocals</code> configuration have symmetrical APIs, so I will only cover <code>loginLocals</code> here to illustrate how to use both.</p> 
         <p>You can configure this parameter in one of <em>3</em> ways. Why 3? Because there are 3 types of ways that you can retrieve your locals.</p> 
         <ol> 
          <li> <p>Static local vars that never change values:</p> <pre><code>```javascript
everyauth.password.loginLocals({
  title: 'Login'
});
```
</code></pre> </li> 
          <li> <p>Dynamic synchronous local vars that depend on the incoming request, but whose values are retrieved synchronously</p> <pre><code>```javascript
everyauth.password.loginLocals( function (req, res) {
  var sess = req.session;
  return {
    isReturning: sess.isReturning
  };
});
```
</code></pre> </li> 
          <li> <p>Dynamic asynchronous local vars</p> <pre><code>```javascript
everyauth.password.loginLocals( function (req, res, done) {
  asyncCall( function ( err, data) {
    if (err) return done(err);
    done(null, {
      title: il8n.titleInLanguage('Login Page', il8n.language(data.geo))
    });
  });
});
```
</code></pre> </li> 
         </ol> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-password-recipe-4-customize-your-registration-validation" class="anchor" href="#password-recipe-4-customize-your-registration-validation" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Password Recipe 4: Customize Your Registration Validation</h3> 
         <p>By default, <code>everyauth.password</code> automatically</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li>validates that the login (or email or phone, depending on what you authenticate with -- see Password Recipe 2) is present in the login http request,</li> 
          <li>validates that the password is present</li> 
          <li>validates that an email login is a correctly formatted email</li> 
          <li>validates that a phone login is a valid phone number</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>If any of these validations fail, then the appropriate errors are generated and accessible to you in your view via the <code>errors</code> view local variable.</p> 
         <p>If you want to add additional validations beyond this, you can do so by configuring the step, <code>validateRegistration</code>:</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">validateRegistration</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">newUserAttributes</span>, <span class="pl-smi">baseErrors</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Here, newUserAttributes is the hash of parameters extracted from the incoming request.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> baseErrors is the array of errors generated by the default automatic validation outlined above</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>   in this same recipe.</span>

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> First, validate your errors. Here, validateUser is a made up function</span>
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> moreErrors <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-en">validateUser</span>( newUserAttributes );
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-smi">moreErrors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">length</span>) <span class="pl-smi">baseErrors</span>.<span class="pl-smi">push</span>.<span class="pl-c1">apply</span>(baseErrors, moreErrors);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Return the array of errors, so your view has access to them.</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> baseErrors;
  });</pre>
         </div> 
         <h3><a id="user-content-password-recipe-5-password-hashing" class="anchor" href="#password-recipe-5-password-hashing" aria-hidden="true">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Password Recipe 5: Password Hashing</h3> 
         <p>By default, everyauth is agnostic about how you decide to store your users and therefore passwords. However, one should <em>always</em> use password hashing and salting for security.</p> 
         <p>Here's an example of how to incorporate password hashing into everyauth using bcrypt hashing. The idea is to store a salt and hash value inside your user object instead of the password. The hash value is generated from the password (sent with a registration or login request) and unique salt per user, using the bcrypt algorithm.</p> 
         <div class="highlight highlight-source-js">
          <pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Make sure to `npm install bcrypt`</span>
<span class="pl-k">var</span> bcrypt <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>bcrypt<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">registerUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">newUserAttrs</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> promise <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">this</span>.<span class="pl-en">Promise</span>()
      , password <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttrs</span>.<span class="pl-smi">password</span>;

    <span class="pl-k">delete</span> newUserAttrs[password]; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Don't store password</span>
    <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttrs</span>.<span class="pl-smi">salt</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">bcrypt</span>.<span class="pl-en">genSaltSync</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>);
    <span class="pl-smi">newUserAttrs</span>.<span class="pl-c1">hash</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">bcrypt</span>.<span class="pl-en">hashSync</span>(password, salt);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Create a new user in your data store</span>
    <span class="pl-en">createUser</span>( newUserAttrs, <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">err</span>, <span class="pl-smi">createdUser</span>) {
      <span class="pl-k">if</span> (err) <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fail</span>(err);
      <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fulfill</span>(createdUser);
    });

    <span class="pl-k">return</span> promise;
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">authenticate</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">login</span>, <span class="pl-smi">password</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> promise
      , errors <span class="pl-k">=</span> [];
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-k">!</span>login) <span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Missing login.<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-k">!</span>password) <span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Missing password.<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">length</span>) <span class="pl-k">return</span> errors;

    promise <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">this</span>.<span class="pl-en">Promise</span>();

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> findUser passes an error or user to a callback after finding the</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> user by login</span>
    <span class="pl-en">findUser</span>( login, <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">err</span>, <span class="pl-smi">user</span>) {
      <span class="pl-k">if</span> (err) {
        <span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-smi">err</span>.<span class="pl-smi">message</span> <span class="pl-k">||</span> err);
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fulfill</span>(errors);
      }
      <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-k">!</span>user) {
        <span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>User with login <span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> <span class="pl-k">+</span> login <span class="pl-k">+</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span> does not exist.<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fulfill</span>(errors);
      }
      <span class="pl-smi">bcrypt</span>.<span class="pl-en">compare</span>(password, <span class="pl-smi">user</span>.<span class="pl-c1">hash</span>, <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">err</span>, <span class="pl-smi">didSucceed</span>) {
        <span class="pl-k">if</span> (err) {
          <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fail</span>(err);
          <span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Wrong password.<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
          <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fulfill</span>(errors);
        }
        <span class="pl-k">if</span> (didSucceed) <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fulfill</span>(user);
        <span class="pl-smi">errors</span>.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Wrong password.<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-smi">promise</span>.<span class="pl-en">fulfill</span>(errors);
      });
    });

    <span class="pl-k">return</span> promise;
  })</pre>
         </div>

    <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>()

  .<span class="pl-en">appSecret</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>YOUR CLIENT SECRET HERE<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
  .<span class="pl-c1">scope</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>https://www.google.com/m8/feeds<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> What you want access to</span>
  .<span class="pl-en">handleAuthCallbackError</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">req</span>, <span class="pl-smi">res</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> If a user denies your app, Google will redirect the user to</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> /auth/facebook/callback?error=access_denied</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> This configurable route handler defines how you want to respond to</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> that.</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> If you do not configure this, everyauth renders a default fallback</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> view notifying the user that their authentication failed and why.</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">findOrCreateUser</span>( <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">session</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessToken</span>, <span class="pl-smi">accessTokenExtra</span>, <span class="pl-smi">googleUserMetadata</span>) {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> find or create user logic goes here</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Return a user or Promise that promises a user</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Promises are created via</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>     var promise = this.Promise();</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">redirectPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">routes</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> (<span class="pl-smi">app</span>) {
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Define your routes here</span>
};

<span class="pl-en">connect</span>(
    <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">cookieParser</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">session</span>({secret<span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>whodunnit<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>})
  , <span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">middleware</span>()
  , <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">router</span>(routes);
).<span class="pl-en">listen</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3000</span>);</pre>
         </div>

          <pre><span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-smi">readability</span>.<span class="pl-en">configurable</span>();</pre>

         <h3><a id="user-content-dropbox-oauth" class="anchor" href="#dropbox-oauth" aria-hidden="true">

          <pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> everyauth <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">require</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>everyauth<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> return usersByDropboxId[user.uid] || (usersByDropboxId[user.uid] = user);</span>
  })
  .<span class="pl-en">redirectPath</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>);

};

    <span class="pl-smi">connect</span>.<span class="pl-en">bodyParser</span>()

  , <span class="pl-smi">everyauth</span>.<span class="pl-en">middleware</span>()
